Section 1:
SENATE MINORITY REPORT
AMENDMENTS TO
SENATE BILL 1507
By Nonconcurring Members of COMMITTEE ON FINANCE AND REVENUE
February 13
1 On page 1 of the printed bill, line 2, after “amending” delete the rest of the line and insert
2 “ORS 178.300, 178.375, 238A.005, 238A.125, 238A.150, 238A.170, 238A.230, 238A.370, 238A.400,
3 238A.410, 238A.415, 238A.430, 238A.435, 305.239, 305.494, 305.690, 305.842, 314.011, 314.306, 315.004,
4 315.266, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097, 317A.100, 458.670, 657.010 and 657B.010;”.
5 Delete lines 5 through 27 and delete pages 2 through 5 and insert:
6 “SECTION 1. ORS 178.300 is amended to read:
7 “178.300. As used in ORS 178.300 to 178.360:
8 “(1) ‘Account’ means an individual account established in accordance with ORS 178.300 to
9 178.360.
10 “(2) ‘Account owner’ means the person who has the right to withdraw funds from the account.
11 The account owner may also be the designated beneficiary of the account.
12 “(3) ‘Board’ means the Oregon 529 Savings Board established under ORS 178.310.
13 “(4) ‘Designated beneficiary’ means, except as provided in ORS 178.350, the individual designated
14 at the time the account is opened as having the right to receive a qualified withdrawal for the
15 payment of qualified higher education expenses, or if the designated beneficiary is replaced in ac-
16 cordance with ORS 178.350, the replacement.
17 “(5) ‘Financial institution’ means a bank, a commercial bank, a national bank, a savings bank,
18 a savings and loan, a thrift institution, a credit union, an insurance company, a trust company, a
19 mutual fund, an investment firm or other similar entity authorized to do business in this state.
20 “(6) ‘Higher education institution’ means an eligible education institution as defined in section
21 529(e)(5) of the Internal Revenue Code.
22 “(7) ‘Internal Revenue Code’ means the federal Internal Revenue Code as amended and in effect
23 on December 31, [2023] 2025.
24 “(8) ‘Member of the family’ shall have the same meaning as contained in section 529(e) of the
25 Internal Revenue Code.
26 “(9) ‘Network’ means the Oregon 529 Savings Network established under ORS 178.305.
27 “(10) ‘Nonqualified withdrawal’ means a withdrawal from an account that is not a qualified
28 withdrawal.
29 “(11) ‘Qualified higher education expenses’ means tuition and other permitted expenses as set
30 forth in section 529(e) of the Internal Revenue Code for the enrollment or attendance of a designated
31 beneficiary at a higher education institution, expenses associated with registered apprenticeship
32 programs described in section 529(c)(8) of the Internal Revenue Code and amounts paid as principal
33 or interest on a qualified education loan to the extent allowed under section 529(c)(9) of the Internal
34 Revenue Code.
LC 302/SB 1507-MR8
1 “(12) ‘Qualified withdrawal’ means a withdrawal made as prescribed under ORS 178.355 and
2 made:
3 “(a) From an account to pay the qualified higher education expenses of the designated benefi-
4 ciary;
5 “(b) As the result of the death or disability of the designated beneficiary;
6 “(c) As the result of a scholarship, allowance or payment described in section 135(d)(1)(A), (B)
7 or (C) of the Internal Revenue Code that is received by the designated beneficiary, but only to the
8 extent of the amount of the scholarship, allowance or payment; or
9 “(d) As a rollover or change in the designated beneficiary described in ORS 178.350.
10 “SECTION 2. ORS 178.375 is amended to read:
11 “178.375. As used in this section and ORS 178.380 and 178.385:
12 “(1) ‘ABLE account’ means an account established by an eligible individual, owned by the eli-
13 gible individual and maintained under the qualified ABLE program established by the Oregon 529
14 Savings Board under ORS 178.380.
15 “(2) ‘ABLE Act’ means the Stephen Beck, Jr., Achieving a Better Life Experience Act of 2014
16 (Division B of P.L. 113-295).
17 “(3) ‘Designated beneficiary’ has the same meaning as contained in section 529A of the Internal
18 Revenue Code.
19 “(4) ‘Eligible individual’ has the same meaning as contained in section 529A of the Internal Re-
20 venue Code.
21 “(5) ‘Internal Revenue Code’ means the federal Internal Revenue Code as amended and in effect
22 on December 31, [2023] 2025.
23 “(6) ‘Qualified disability expense’ has the same meaning as contained in section 529A of the
24 Internal Revenue Code.
25 “SECTION 3. ORS 238A.005 is amended to read:
26 “238A.005. For the purposes of this chapter:
27 “(1) ‘Active member’ means a member of the pension program or the individual account program
28 of the Oregon Public Service Retirement Plan who is actively employed in a qualifying position.
29 “(2) ‘Actuarial equivalent’ means a payment or series of payments having the same value as the
30 payment or series of payments replaced, computed on the basis of interest rate and mortality as-
31 sumptions adopted by the board.
32 “(3) ‘Board’ means the Public Employees Retirement Board.
33 “(4) ‘Eligible employee’ means a person who performs services for a participating public em-
34 ployer, including persons considered employees of a participating public employer under 26 U.S.C.
35 3121(d)(2), as in effect on January 1, [2024] 2026, and elected officials other than judges. ‘Eligible
36 employee’ does not include:
37 “(a) Persons engaged as independent contractors;
38 “(b) Aliens working under a training or educational visa;
39 “(c) Persons provided sheltered employment or make-work by a public employer;
40 “(d) Persons categorized by a participating public employer as student employees;
41 “(e) Any person who is in custody in a state institution;
42 “(f) Employees of foreign trade offices of the Oregon Business Development Department who live
43 and perform services in foreign countries under the provisions of ORS 285A.075 (1)(g);
44 “(g) An employee actively participating in an alternative retirement program established under
45 ORS 353.250 or an optional retirement plan established under ORS 341.551;
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 2
1 “(h) Employees of a public university listed in ORS 352.002 who are actively participating in an
2 optional retirement plan offered under ORS 243.815;
3 “(i) Persons employed in positions classified as post-doctoral scholar positions by a public uni-
4 versity listed in ORS 352.002, or by the Oregon Health and Science University, under ORS 350.370;
5 “(j) Any employee who belongs to a class of employees that was not eligible on August 28, 2003,
6 for membership in the system under the provisions of ORS chapter 238 or other law;
7 “(k) Any person who belongs to a class of employees who are not eligible to become members
8 of the Oregon Public Service Retirement Plan under the provisions of ORS 238A.070 (2);
9 “(L) Any person who is retired under ORS 238A.100 to 238A.250 or ORS chapter 238 and who
10 continues to receive retirement benefits while employed; and
11 “(m) Judges.
12 “(5) ‘Firefighter’ means:
13 “(a) A person employed by a local government, as defined in ORS 174.116, whose primary job
14 duties include the fighting of fires;
15 “(b) The State Fire Marshal, chief deputy state fire marshals and deputy state fire marshals;
16 “(c) An employee of the State Fire Marshal whose primary duties include fire investigation, fire
17 prevention, fire safety, fire control or fire suppression;
18 “(d) An employee of the State Forestry Department who is certified by the State Forester as a
19 professional wildland firefighter and whose primary duties include the abatement of uncontrolled
20 fires as described in ORS 477.064; and
21 “(e) An employee of the Oregon Military Department whose primary duties include fighting
22 structural, aircraft, wildland or other fires.
23 “(6) ‘Fund’ means the Public Employees Retirement Fund.
24 “(7)(a) ‘Hour of service’ means:
25 “(A) An hour for which an eligible employee is directly or indirectly paid or entitled to payment
26 by a participating public employer for performance of duties in a qualifying position; and
27 “(B) An hour of vacation, holiday, illness, incapacity, jury duty, military duty or authorized
28 leave during which an employee does not perform duties but for which the employee is directly or
29 indirectly paid or entitled to payment by a participating public employer for services in a qualifying
30 position, as long as the hour is within the number of hours regularly scheduled for the performance
31 of duties during the period of vacation, holiday, illness, incapacity, jury duty, military duty or au-
32 thorized leave.
33 “(b) ‘Hour of service’ does not include any hour for which payment is made or due under a plan
34 maintained solely for the purpose of complying with applicable unemployment compensation laws.
35 “(8) ‘Inactive member’ means a member of the pension program or the individual account pro-
36 gram of the Oregon Public Service Retirement Plan whose membership has not been terminated, who
37 is not a retired member and who is not employed in a qualifying position.
38 “(9) ‘Individual account program’ means the defined contribution individual account program of
39 the Oregon Public Service Retirement Plan established under ORS 238A.025.
40 “(10) ‘Institution of higher education’ means a public university listed in ORS 352.002, the
41 Oregon Health and Science University or a community college, as defined in ORS 341.005.
42 “(11) ‘Member’ means an eligible employee who has established membership in the pension pro-
43 gram or the individual account program of the Oregon Public Service Retirement Plan and whose
44 membership has not been terminated under ORS 238A.110 or 238A.310.
45 “(12) ‘Participating public employer’ means a public employer as defined in ORS 238.005 that
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 3
1 provides retirement benefits for employees of the public employer under the system.
2 “(13) ‘Pension program’ means the defined benefit pension program of the Oregon Public Service
3 Retirement Plan established under ORS 238A.025.
4 “(14) ‘Police officer’ means a police officer as described in ORS 238.005.
5 “(15) ‘Qualifying position’ means one or more jobs with one or more participating public em-
6 ployers in which an eligible employee performs 600 or more hours of service in a full calendar year,
7 or would perform 600 or more hours of service if the employee were employed for the full calendar
8 year, excluding any service in a job for which benefits are not provided under the Oregon Public
9 Service Retirement Plan pursuant to ORS 238A.070 (2).
10 “(16) ‘Retired member’ means a pension program member who is receiving a pension as provided
11 in ORS 238A.180 to 238A.195.
12 “(17)(a) ‘Salary’ means the remuneration paid to an active member in return for services to the
13 participating public employer, including remuneration in the form of living quarters, board or other
14 items of value, to the extent the remuneration is, or would be if the member were an Oregon resi-
15 dent, includable in the employee’s taxable income under Oregon law. ‘Salary’ includes the additional
16 amounts specified in paragraph (b) of this subsection, but does not include the amounts specified in
17 paragraph (c) of this subsection, regardless of whether those amounts are includable in taxable in-
18 come.
19 “(b) ‘Salary’ includes the following amounts:
20 “(A) Payments of employee and employer money into a deferred compensation plan that are
21 made at the election of the employee.
22 “(B) Contributions to a tax-sheltered or deferred annuity that are made at the election of the
23 employee.
24 “(C) Any amount that is contributed to a cafeteria plan or qualified transportation fringe benefit
25 plan by the employer at the election of the employee and that is not includable in the taxable in-
26 come of the employee by reason of 26 U.S.C. 125 or 132(f)(4), as in effect on December 31, [2023]
27 2025.
28 “(D) Any amount that is contributed to a cash or deferred arrangement by the employer at the
29 election of the employee and that is not included in the taxable income of the employee by reason
30 of 26 U.S.C. 402(e)(3), as in effect on December 31, [2023] 2025.
31 “(E) Retroactive payments described in ORS 238.008.
32 “(F) The amount of an employee contribution to the individual account program that is paid by
33 the employer and deducted from the compensation of the employee, as provided under ORS 238A.335
34 (1) and (2)(a).
35 “(G) The amount of an employee contribution to the individual account program that is not paid
36 by the employer under ORS 238A.335.
37 “(H) Wages of a deceased member paid to a surviving spouse or dependent children under ORS
38 652.190.
39 “(c) ‘Salary’ does not include the following amounts:
40 “(A) Travel or any other expenses incidental to employer’s business which is reimbursed by the
41 employer.
42 “(B) Payments made on account of an employee’s death.
43 “(C) Any lump sum payment for accumulated unused sick leave, vacation leave or other paid
44 leave.
45 “(D) Any severance payment, accelerated payment of an employment contract for a future period
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 4
1 or advance against future wages.
2 “(E) Any retirement incentive, retirement bonus or retirement gratuitous payment.
3 “(F) Payment for a leave of absence after the date the employer and employee have agreed that
4 no future services in a qualifying position will be performed.
5 “(G) Payments for instructional services rendered to public universities listed in ORS 352.002
6 or the Oregon Health and Science University when those services are in excess of full-time em-
7 ployment subject to this chapter. A person employed under a contract for less than 12 months is
8 subject to this subparagraph only for the months covered by the contract.
9 “(H) The amount of an employee contribution to the individual account program that is paid by
10 the employer and is not deducted from the compensation of the employee, as provided under ORS
11 238A.335 (1) and (2)(b).
12 “(I) Compensation described and authorized under ORS 341.556 that is not paid by the commu-
13 nity college employing the faculty member.
14 “(J) Compensation described and authorized under ORS 352.232 that is not paid by the public
15 university employing the officer or employee.
16 “(K) Compensation described and authorized under ORS 353.270 that is not paid by Oregon
17 Health and Science University.
18 “(L) For years before 2020, any amount in excess of $200,000 for a calendar year. If any period
19 over which salary is determined is less than 12 months, the $200,000 limitation for that period shall
20 be multiplied by a fraction, the numerator of which is the number of months in the determination
21 period and the denominator of which is 12. The board shall adopt rules adjusting this dollar limit
22 to incorporate cost-of-living adjustments authorized by the Internal Revenue Service.
23 “(M) For years beginning on or after January 1, 2020, any amount in excess of $195,000 for a
24 calendar year. If any period over which salary is determined is less than 12 months, the $195,000
25 limitation for that period shall be multiplied by a fraction, the numerator of which is the number
26 of months in the determination period and the denominator of which is 12. On January 1 of each
27 year, the board shall adjust the dollar limit provided by this subparagraph to reflect any percentage
28 changes in the Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers, West Region (All Items), as pub-
29 lished by the Bureau of Labor Statistics of the United States Department of Labor.
30 “(18) ‘System’ means the Public Employees Retirement System.
31 “(19) ‘Workers’ compensation benefits’ means:
32 “(a) Payments made under ORS chapter 656; or
33 “(b) Payments provided in lieu of workers’ compensation benefits under ORS 656.027 (6).

7 “SECTION 5. ORS 238A.125 is amended to read:
8 “238A.125. (1) Upon retiring at normal retirement age, a vested pension program member shall
9 be paid an annual pension for the life of the member as follows:
10 “(a) For service as a police officer or firefighter, 1.8 percent of final average salary multiplied
11 by the number of years of retirement credit attributable to service as a police officer or firefighter.
12 “(b) For service as other than a police officer or firefighter, 1.5 percent of final average salary
13 multiplied by the number of years of retirement credit attributable to service as other than a police
14 officer or firefighter.
15 “(2) Notwithstanding any provision of ORS 238A.100 to 238A.250, the annual benefit payable to
16 a member under the pension program and under any other tax-qualified defined benefit plan main-
17 tained by the participating public employer may not exceed the applicable limitations set forth in
18 26 U.S.C. 415(b), as in effect on December 31, [2023] 2025. The Public Employees Retirement Board
19 shall adopt rules for the administration of this limitation, including adjustments in the annual dollar
20 limitation to reflect cost-of-living adjustments authorized by the Internal Revenue Service.
21 “(3) The board shall make no actuarial adjustment in a member’s pension calculated under this
22 section by reason of the member’s retirement after normal retirement age.
23 “SECTION 6. ORS 238A.125, as amended by section 3, chapter 101, Oregon Laws 2024, is
24 amended to read:
25 “238A.125. (1) Upon retiring at normal retirement age, a vested pension program member shall
26 be paid an annual pension for the life of the member as follows:
27 “(a) For service as a police officer or firefighter, 1.8 percent of final average salary multiplied
28 by the number of years of retirement credit attributable to service as a police officer or firefighter.
29 “(b) For service in a hazardous position, 1.8 percent of final average salary multiplied by the
30 number of years of retirement credit attributable to service in a hazardous position.
31 “(c) For service as other than a police officer or firefighter or in a hazardous position, 1.5 per-
32 cent of final average salary multiplied by the number of years of retirement credit attributable to
33 service as other than a police officer or firefighter or in a hazardous position.
34 “(2) Notwithstanding any provision of ORS 238A.100 to 238A.250, the annual benefit payable to
35 a member under the pension program and under any other tax-qualified defined benefit plan main-
36 tained by the participating public employer may not exceed the applicable limitations set forth in
37 26 U.S.C. 415(b), as in effect on December 31, [2023] 2025. The Public Employees Retirement Board
38 shall adopt rules for the administration of this limitation, including adjustments in the annual dollar
39 limitation to reflect cost-of-living adjustments authorized by the Internal Revenue Service.
40 “(3) The board shall make no actuarial adjustment in a member’s pension calculated under this

16 “(b) With respect to the tax credits contained in this chapter, any reference to the laws of the
17 United States or to the Internal Revenue Code means the laws of the United States relating to in-
18 come taxes or the Internal Revenue Code as they are amended on or before December 31, [2023]
19 2025, even when the amendments take effect or become operative after that date.
20 “(3) Insofar as is practicable in the administration of this chapter, the Department of Revenue
21 shall apply and follow the administrative and judicial interpretations of the federal income tax law.
22 When a provision of the federal income tax law is the subject of conflicting opinions by two or more
23 federal courts, the department shall follow the rule observed by the United States Commissioner of
24 Internal Revenue until the conflict is resolved. Nothing contained in this section limits the right
25 or duty of the department to audit the return of any taxpayer or to determine any fact relating to
26 the tax liability of any taxpayer.
27 “(4) When portions of the Internal Revenue Code incorporated by reference as provided in sub-
28 section (2) of this section refer to rules or regulations prescribed by the Secretary of the Treasury,
29 then such rules or regulations shall be regarded as rules adopted by the department under and in
30 accordance with the provisions of this chapter, whenever they are prescribed or amended.
31 “(5)(a) When portions of the Internal Revenue Code incorporated by reference as provided in
32 subsection (2) of this section are later corrected by an Act or a Title within an Act of the United
33 States Congress designated as an Act or Title making technical corrections, then notwithstanding
34 the date that the Act or Title becomes law, those portions of the Internal Revenue Code, as so
35 corrected, shall be the portions of the Internal Revenue Code incorporated by reference as provided
36 in subsection (2) of this section and shall take effect, unless otherwise indicated by the Act or Title
37 (in which case the provisions shall take effect as indicated in the Act or Title), as if originally in-
38 cluded in the provisions of the Act being technically corrected. If, on account of this subsection, any
39 adjustment is required to an Oregon return that would otherwise be prevented by operation of law
40 or rule, the adjustment shall be made, notwithstanding any law or rule to the contrary, in the
41 manner provided under ORS 314.135.

26 housing or a preservation project; or
27 “(B) 20 years, for any other type of qualified loan.
28 “(8) The Housing and Community Services Department may certify qualified loans that are eli-
29 gible under subsection (5) of this section if the total credits attributable to all qualified loans eligible
30 for credits under this section and then outstanding do not exceed $35 million for any fiscal year. In
31 making loan certifications under subsection (7) of this section, the Housing and Community Services
32 Department shall attempt to distribute the tax credits statewide, but shall concentrate the tax
33 credits in those areas of the state that are determined by the Oregon Housing Stability Council to
34 have the greatest need for affordable housing.
35 “(9) The tax credit provided for in this section may be taken whether or not:
36 “(a) The financial institution is eligible to take a federal income tax credit under section 42 of
37 the Internal Revenue Code with respect to the project financed by the qualified loan;
38 “(b) The project receives financing from bonds, the interest on which is exempt from federal
39 taxation under section 103 of the Internal Revenue Code; or
40 “(c) The project receives moneys from the Elderly and Disabled Housing Fund under ORS
41 456.535.
42 “(10) For a qualified loan defined in subsection (1)(k)(B) of this section financed through the
43 purchase of bonds, the interest of which is exempt from federal taxation under section 103 of the
44 Internal Revenue Code, the amount of finance charge that would have been charged under sub-
45 section (2)(b) of this section is determined by reference to the finance charge that would have been
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 27
1 charged if the federally tax exempt bonds had been issued and the tax credit under this section did
2 not apply.
3 “(11) A lending institution may sell a qualified loan for which a certification has been executed
4 to a qualified assignee whether or not the lending institution retains servicing of the qualified loan
5 so long as a designated lending institution maintains records, annually verified by a loan servicer,
6 that establish the amount of tax credit earned by the taxpayer throughout each year of eligibility.
7 “(12) Notwithstanding any other provision of law, a lending institution that is a community de-
8 velopment corporation organized under the Oregon Nonprofit Corporation Law may transfer all or
9 part of a tax credit allowed under this section to one or more other lending institutions that are
10 stockholders or members of the community development corporation or that otherwise participate
11 through the community development corporation in the making of one or more qualified loans for
12 which the tax credit under this section is allowed.
13 “(13) The lending institution shall file an annual statement with the Housing and Community
14 Services Department, specifying that it has conformed with all requirements imposed by law to
15 qualify for a tax credit under this section.
16 “(14) Notwithstanding subsection (1)(j) and (m) of this section, a qualified borrower on a loan to
17 finance the construction, development, acquisition or rehabilitation of a manufactured dwelling park
18 under subsection (5)(c) of this section must be:
19 “(a) A nonprofit corporation, manufactured dwelling park nonprofit cooperative, state govern-
20 mental entity, local unit of government as defined in ORS 466.706 or housing authority; or
21 “(b) A nonprofit corporation or housing authority that has a controlling interest in the real
22 property that is financed by a qualified loan. A controlling interest includes a controlling interest
23 in the general partner of a limited partnership that owns the real property.
24 “(15) The Department of Revenue may require that a lending institution that has earned the
25 credit and a lending institution that intends to claim the credit jointly file a notice, as prescribed
26 by the Department of Revenue. The notice must comply with ORS 315.056 (2) or 315.058 (2).
27 “(16) The Housing and Community Services Department shall provide information to the De-
28 partment of Revenue about all certifications executed under this section, if required by ORS 315.058.
29 “(17) The Housing and Community Services Department and the Department of Revenue may
30 adopt rules to carry out the provisions of this section.

27 “(21) ‘Parent’ means:
28 “(a) A biological parent, adoptive parent, stepparent or foster parent of a covered individual;
29 “(b) A person who was a foster parent of a covered individual when the covered individual was
30 a minor;
31 “(c) A person designated as the legal guardian of a covered individual at the time the covered
32 individual was a minor or required a legal guardian;
33 “(d) A person with whom a covered individual was or is in a relationship of in loco parentis;
34 or
35 “(e) A parent of a covered individual’s spouse or domestic partner who meets a description un-
36 der paragraphs (a) to (d) of this subsection.
37 “(22) ‘Safe leave’ means leave taken for any purpose described in ORS 659A.272.
38 “(23) ‘Self-employed individual’ means:
39 “(a) An individual who has self-employment income as defined in section 1402(b) of the Internal
40 Revenue Code as amended and in effect on December 31, [2023] 2025; or
41 “(b) An independent contractor as defined in ORS 670.600.
42 “(24) ‘Serious health condition’ means:
43 “(a) An illness, injury, impairment or physical or mental condition that requires inpatient care
44 in a hospital, hospice or residential medical care facility;
45 “(b) An illness, disease or condition that in the medical judgment of the treating health care
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 45
1 provider poses an imminent danger of death, is terminal in prognosis with a reasonable possibility
2 of death in the near future, or requires constant care;
3 “(c) Any period of disability due to pregnancy, or period of absence for prenatal care; or
4 “(d) Any period of absence for the donation of a body part, organ or tissue, including preoper-
5 ative or diagnostic services, surgery, post-operative treatment and recovery.
6 “(25) ‘Third party administrator’ means a third party that enters into an agreement with the
7 Director of the Employment Department to implement and administer the paid family and medical
8 leave program established under this chapter.
9 “(26) ‘Tribal government’ means:
10 “(a) A tribal government as defined in ORS 181A.940; or
11 “(b) A federally recognized Indian tribe.
12 “(27)(a) ‘Wages’ has the meaning given that term in ORS 657.105.
13 “(b) ‘Wages’ does not mean contribution amounts paid to the Paid Family and Medical Leave
14 Insurance Fund by an employer on behalf of an employee under ORS 657B.150 (5).
15 “SECTION 33. (1) Except as provided in subsections (2) and (3) of this section, the
16 amendments to statutes by sections 1 to 32 of this 2026 Act apply to transactions or activities
17 occurring on or after January 1, 2026, in tax years beginning on or after January 1, 2026.
18 “(2) The effective and applicable dates, and the exceptions, special rules and coordination
19 with the Internal Revenue Code, as amended, relative to those dates, contained in federal law
20 amending the Internal Revenue Code and enacted before January 1, 2026, apply for Oregon
21 personal income and corporate excise and income tax purposes, to the extent they can be
22 made applicable, in the same manner as they are applied under the Internal Revenue Code
23 and related federal law.
24 “(3)(a) If a deficiency is assessed against any taxpayer for a tax year beginning before
25 January 1, 2026, and the deficiency or any portion thereof is attributable to any retroactive
26 treatment under the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239, 305.494, 305.690, 305.842,
27 314.011, 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and 317A.100 by sections 1, 2
28 and 16 to 29 of this 2026 Act, then any interest or penalty assessed under ORS chapter 305,
29 314, 315, 316, 317, 317A or 318 with respect to the deficiency or portion thereof shall be can-
30 celed.
31 “(b) If a refund is due any taxpayer for a tax year beginning before January 1, 2026, and
32 the refund or any portion thereof is due the taxpayer on account of any retroactive treat-
33 ment under the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239, 305.494, 305.690, 305.842, 314.011,
34 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and 317A.100 by sections 1, 2 and 16
35 to 29 of this 2026 Act for a tax year beginning before January 1, 2026, then notwithstanding
36 ORS 305.270 or 314.415 or any other law, the refund or portion thereof shall be paid without
37 interest.
38 “(c) Any changes required because of the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239,
39 305.494, 305.690, 305.842, 314.011, 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and
40 317A.100 by sections 1, 2 and 16 to 29 of this 2026 Act for a tax year beginning before January
41 1, 2026, shall be made by filing an amended return within the time prescribed by law.
42 “(d) If a taxpayer fails to file an amended return under paragraph (c) of this subsection,
43 the Department of Revenue shall make any changes under paragraph (c) of this subsection
44 on the return to which the changes relate within the period specified for issuing a notice of
45 deficiency or claiming a refund as otherwise provided by law with respect to that return, or
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 46
1 within one year after a return for a tax year beginning on or after January 1, 2026, and be-
2 fore January 1, 2027, is filed, whichever period expires later.
3 “SECTION 34. ORS 315.266 is amended to read:
4 “315.266. (1)(a) In addition to any other credit available for purposes of ORS chapter 316, an
5 eligible resident individual shall be allowed a credit against the tax otherwise due under ORS
6 chapter 316 for the tax year in an amount equal to [nine] 14 percent of the earned income credit
7 allowable to the individual for the same tax year under section 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
8 “(b) Notwithstanding paragraph (a) of this subsection, for a taxpayer with a dependent under the
9 age of three at the close of the tax year, the credit allowed under this section shall be in an amount
10 equal to [12] 17 percent of the earned income credit allowable to the individual for the same tax
11 year under section 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
12 “(2) A resident individual may claim a credit under this section, using either a Social Security
13 number or an individual taxpayer identification number, if, but for section 32(m) of the Internal
14 Revenue Code, the individual would otherwise be eligible to claim a credit under section 32 of the
15 Internal Revenue Code. The credit allowed as provided in this subsection shall equal the percent-
16 age, as stated in subsection (1) of this section, of the amount that would be allowed on a federal
17 return, based on the amount of the individual’s earned income and the other provisions of section
18 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
19 “(3) An eligible nonresident individual shall be allowed the credit computed in the same manner
20 and subject to the same limitations as the credit allowed a resident by subsection (1) or (2) of this
21 section. However, the credit shall be prorated using the proportion provided in ORS 316.117.
22 “(4) If a change in the taxable year of a taxpayer occurs as described in ORS 314.085, or if the
23 Department of Revenue terminates the taxpayer’s taxable year under ORS 314.440, the credit al-
24 lowed by this section shall be prorated or computed in a manner consistent with ORS 314.085.
25 “(5) If a change in the status of a taxpayer from resident to nonresident or from nonresident to
26 resident occurs, the credit allowed by this section shall be determined in a manner consistent with
27 ORS 316.117.
28 “(6) If the amount allowable as a credit under this section, when added to the sum of the
29 amounts allowable as payment of tax under ORS 316.187 or 316.583, other tax prepayment amounts
30 and other refundable credit amounts, exceeds the taxes imposed by ORS chapters 314 and 316 for
31 the tax year after application of any nonrefundable credits allowable for purposes of ORS chapter
32 316 for the tax year, the amount of the excess shall be refunded to the taxpayer as provided in ORS
33 316.502.
34 “(7) The Department of Revenue may adopt rules for purposes of this section, including but not
35 limited to rules relating to proof of eligibility, the furnishing of information regarding the federal
36 earned income credit claimed by the taxpayer for the tax year and policies and guidelines for the
37 determination of the amount of credit allowed under subsection (2) of this section.
38 “(8) Refunds attributable to the earned income credit allowed under this section do not bear
39 interest.
40 “SECTION 35. The amendments to ORS 315.266 by section 34 of this 2026 Act apply to tax
41 years beginning on or after January 1, 2026.
42 “SECTION 36. This 2026 Act takes effect on the 91st day after the date on which the 2026
43 regular session of the Eighty-third Legislative Assembly adjourns sine die.”.

6 “SECTION 1. ORS 178.300 is amended to read:
7 “178.300. As used in ORS 178.300 to 178.360:
8 “(1) ‘Account’ means an individual account established in accordance with ORS 178.300 to
9 178.360.
10 “(2) ‘Account owner’ means the person who has the right to withdraw funds from the account.
11 The account owner may also be the designated beneficiary of the account.
12 “(3) ‘Board’ means the Oregon 529 Savings Board established under ORS 178.310.
13 “(4) ‘Designated beneficiary’ means, except as provided in ORS 178.350, the individual designated
14 at the time the account is opened as having the right to receive a qualified withdrawal for the
15 payment of qualified higher education expenses, or if the designated beneficiary is replaced in ac-
16 cordance with ORS 178.350, the replacement.
17 “(5) ‘Financial institution’ means a bank, a commercial bank, a national bank, a savings bank,
18 a savings and loan, a thrift institution, a credit union, an insurance company, a trust company, a
19 mutual fund, an investment firm or other similar entity authorized to do business in this state.
20 “(6) ‘Higher education institution’ means an eligible education institution as defined in section
21 529(e)(5) of the Internal Revenue Code.
22 “(7) ‘Internal Revenue Code’ means the federal Internal Revenue Code as amended and in effect
23 on December 31, [2023] 2025.
24 “(8) ‘Member of the family’ shall have the same meaning as contained in section 529(e) of the
25 Internal Revenue Code.
26 “(9) ‘Network’ means the Oregon 529 Savings Network established under ORS 178.305.
27 “(10) ‘Nonqualified withdrawal’ means a withdrawal from an account that is not a qualified
28 withdrawal.
29 “(11) ‘Qualified higher education expenses’ means tuition and other permitted expenses as set
30 forth in section 529(e) of the Internal Revenue Code for the enrollment or attendance of a designated
31 beneficiary at a higher education institution, expenses associated with registered apprenticeship
32 programs described in section 529(c)(8) of the Internal Revenue Code and amounts paid as principal
33 or interest on a qualified education loan to the extent allowed under section 529(c)(9) of the Internal
34 Revenue Code.

23 is 80 percent or less of area median income as defined in ORS 458.610.
24 “(m) ‘Sponsoring entity’ means a nonprofit corporation, nonprofit cooperative, state govern-
25 mental entity, local unit of government as defined in ORS 466.706, housing authority or any other
26 person, provided that the person has agreed to restrictive covenants imposed by a nonprofit corpo-
27 ration, nonprofit cooperative, state governmental entity, local unit of government or housing au-
28 thority.
29 “(2) The Department of Revenue shall allow a credit against taxes otherwise due under this
30 chapter for the tax year to a lending institution that makes a qualified loan certified by the Housing
31 and Community Services Department as provided in subsection (7) of this section. The amount of the
32 credit is equal to the difference between:
33 “(a) The amount of finance charge charged by the lending institution during the tax year at an
34 annual rate less than the market rate for a qualified loan that complies with the requirements of this
35 section; and
36 “(b) The amount of finance charge that would have been charged during the tax year by the
37 lending institution for the qualified loan for housing construction, development, acquisition or re-
38 habilitation measured at the annual rate charged by the lending institution for nonsubsidized loans
39 made under like terms and conditions at the time the qualified loan for housing construction, de-
40 velopment, acquisition or rehabilitation is made.
41 “(3) The maximum amount of credit for the difference between the amounts described in sub-
42 section (2)(a) and (b) of this section may not exceed four percent of the average unpaid balance of
43 the qualified loan during the tax year for which the credit is claimed.
44 “(4) Any tax credit allowed under this section that is not used by the taxpayer in a particular
45 year may be carried forward and offset against the taxpayer’s tax liability for the next succeeding
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 25

1 tax year. Any credit remaining unused in the next succeeding tax year may be carried forward and
2 used in the second succeeding tax year, and likewise, any credit not used in that second succeeding
3 tax year may be carried forward and used in the third succeeding tax year, and any credit not used
4 in that third succeeding tax year may be carried forward and used in the fourth succeeding tax year,
5 and any credit not used in that fourth succeeding tax year may be carried forward and used in the
6 fifth succeeding tax year, but may not be carried forward for any tax year thereafter.
7 “(5) To be eligible for the tax credit allowable under this section, a lending institution must
8 make a qualified loan by either purchasing bonds, the proceeds of which are used to finance or re-
9 finance a loan that meets the criteria stated in this subsection, or making a loan directly to:
10 “(a) An individual or individuals who own a dwelling, participate in an owner-occupied commu-
11 nity rehabilitation program and are certified by the local government or its designated agent as
12 having an income level when the loan is made of 80 percent of the area median income or less;
13 “(b) A qualified borrower who:
14 “(A) Uses the loan proceeds to finance construction, development, acquisition or rehabilitation
15 of housing, including housing in the form of a limited equity cooperative; and
16 “(B) Provides a written certification executed by the Housing and Community Services Depart-
17 ment that the:
18 “(i) Housing created by the loan is or will be occupied by households earning 80 percent of the
19 area median income or less; and
20 “(ii) Full amount of savings from the reduced interest rate provided by the lending institution
21 is or will be passed on, in the form of reduced housing payments, to the tenants or to the holders
22 of proprietary leases in a limited equity cooperative;
23 “(c) Subject to subsection (14) of this section, a qualified borrower who:
24 “(A) Uses the loan proceeds to finance construction, development, acquisition or rehabilitation
25 of housing consisting of a manufactured dwelling park; and
26 “(B) Provides a written certification executed by the Housing and Community Services Depart-
27 ment that the housing will continue to be operated as a manufactured dwelling park during the pe-
28 riod for which the tax credit is allowed;
29 “(d) A qualified borrower who:
30 “(A) Uses the loan proceeds to finance acquisition or rehabilitation of housing consisting of a
31 preservation project; and
32 “(B) Provides a written certification executed by the Housing and Community Services Depart-
33 ment that the housing preserved by the loan:
34 “(i) Is or will be occupied by households earning 80 percent of the area median income or less;
35 and
36 “(ii) Is the subject of a rent assistance contract with the United States Department of Housing
37 and Urban Development or the United States Department of Agriculture that will be maintained by
38 the qualified borrower;
39 “(e) A qualified borrower who:
40 “(A) Uses the loan proceeds to finance construction, development, acquisition or rehabilitation
41 of housing; and
42 “(B) Provides a written certification executed by the Housing and Community Services Depart-
43 ment or the governmental party to the rent assistance contract that the housing preserved by the
44 loan:
45 “(i) Is or will be occupied by households earning 80 percent of the area median income or less;
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 26

1 and
2 “(ii) Is the subject of a rent assistance contract with the federal government or with a state or

34 have the greatest need for affordable housing.

26 on which family leave, medical leave or safe leave commences.
27 “(6) ‘Child’ means:
28 “(a) A biological child, adopted child, stepchild or foster child of a covered individual or of the
29 covered individual’s spouse or domestic partner;
30 “(b) A person who is or was a legal ward of a covered individual or of the covered individual’s
31 spouse or domestic partner; or
32 “(c) A person who is or was in a relationship of in loco parentis with a covered individual or
33 with the covered individual’s spouse or domestic partner.
34 “(7) ‘Claimant’ means an individual who has submitted an application or established a claim for
35 benefits.
36 “(8) ‘Contribution’ or ‘contributions’ means the money payments made by any of the following
37 under ORS 657B.150:
38 “(a) An employer;
39 “(b) An employee;
40 “(c) A self-employed individual;
41 “(d) A tribal government; or
42 “(e) An employee of a tribal government.
43 “(9) ‘Covered individual’ means any one of the following who qualifies under ORS 657B.015 to
44 receive family and medical leave insurance benefits:
45 “(a) An eligible employee;
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 43

1 “(b) A self-employed individual; or
2 “(c) An employee of a tribal government.
3 “(10) ‘Domestic partner’ means an individual joined in a domestic partnership.
4 “(11) ‘Domestic partnership’ has the meaning given that term in ORS 106.310.
5 “(12) ‘Eligible employee’ means:
6 “(a)(A) An employee who has earned at least $1,000 in wages during the base year; or
7 “(B) If an employee has not earned at least $1,000 in wages during the base year, an employee
8 who has earned at least $1,000 in wages during the alternate base year; and
9 “(b) An employee to whom paid family and medical leave insurance benefits may be available
10 under ORS 657B.015.
11 “(13) ‘Eligible employee’s average weekly wage’ means an amount calculated by the Director of
12 the Employment Department by dividing the total wages earned by an eligible employee during the
13 base year by the number of weeks in the base year.
14 “(14)(a) ‘Employee’ means:
15 “(A) An individual performing services for an employer for remuneration or under any contract
16 of hire, written or oral, express or implied.
17 “(B) A home care worker as defined in ORS 410.600.
18 “(b) ‘Employee’ does not include:
19 “(A) An independent contractor as defined in ORS 670.600.
20 “(B) A participant in a work training program administered under a state or federal assistance
21 program.
22 “(C) A participant in a work-study program that provides students in secondary or
23 postsecondary educational institutions with employment opportunities for financial assistance or
24 vocational training.
25 “(D) A railroad worker exempted under the federal Railroad Unemployment Insurance Act.
26 “(E) A volunteer.
27 “(F) A judge as defined in ORS 260.005.
28 “(G) A member of the Legislative Assembly.
29 “(H) A holder of public office as defined in ORS 260.005.
30 “(15)(a) ‘Employer’ means any person that employs one or more employees working anywhere in
31 this state or any agent or employee of such person to whom the duties of the person under this
32 chapter have been delegated.
33 “(b) ‘Employer’ includes:
34 “(A) A political subdivision of this state or any county, city, district, authority or public corpo-
35 ration, or any instrumentality of a county, city, district, authority or public corporation, organized
36 and existing under law or charter;
37 “(B) An individual;
38 “(C) Any type of organization, corporation, partnership, limited liability company, association,
39 trust, estate, joint stock company or insurance company;
40 “(D) Any successor in interest to an entity described in subparagraph (C) of this paragraph;
41 “(E) A trustee, trustee in bankruptcy or receiver; or
42 “(F) A trustee or legal representative of a deceased person.
43 “(c) ‘Employer’ does not include the federal government or a tribal government.
44 “(16) ‘Employment agency’ has the meaning given that term in ORS 658.005.
45 “(17) ‘Family and medical leave insurance benefits’ means the wage replacement benefits that
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 44

1 are available to a covered individual under ORS 657B.050 or under the terms of an employer plan
2 approved under ORS 657B.210, for family leave, medical leave or safe leave.
3 “(18)(a) ‘Family leave’ means leave from work taken by a covered individual:
4 “(A) To care for and bond with a child during the first year after the child’s birth or during the
5 first year after the placement of the child through foster care or adoption;
6 “(B) To effectuate the legal process required for placement of a foster child or the adoption of
7 a child; or
8 “(C) To care for a family member with a serious health condition.
9 “(b) ‘Family leave’ does not mean:
10 “(A) Leave described in ORS 659A.159 (1)(a) except for leave to care for a child who requires
11 home care due to an illness, injury or condition that is a serious health condition;
12 “(B) Leave described in ORS 659A.159 (1)(b); or
13 “(C) Leave authorized under ORS 659A.093.
14 “(19) ‘Family member’ means:
15 “(a) The spouse of a covered individual;
16 “(b) A child or the child’s spouse or domestic partner;
17 “(c) A parent or the parent’s spouse or domestic partner;
18 “(d) A sibling or stepsibling of a covered individual or the sibling’s or stepsibling’s spouse or
19 domestic partner;
20 “(e) A grandparent of a covered individual or the grandparent’s spouse or domestic partner;
21 “(f) A grandchild of a covered individual or the grandchild’s spouse or domestic partner;
22 “(g) The domestic partner of a covered individual; or
23 “(h) Any individual related by blood or affinity whose close association with a covered individ-
24 ual is the equivalent of a family relationship.
25 “(20) ‘Medical leave’ means leave from work taken by a covered individual that is made neces-
26 sary by the individual’s own serious health condition.
27 “(21) ‘Parent’ means:
28 “(a) A biological parent, adoptive parent, stepparent or foster parent of a covered individual;
29 “(b) A person who was a foster parent of a covered individual when the covered individual was
30 a minor;
31 “(c) A person designated as the legal guardian of a covered individual at the time the covered
32 individual was a minor or required a legal guardian;
33 “(d) A person with whom a covered individual was or is in a relationship of in loco parentis;
34 or
35 “(e) A parent of a covered individual’s spouse or domestic partner who meets a description un-
36 der paragraphs (a) to (d) of this subsection.
37 “(22) ‘Safe leave’ means leave taken for any purpose described in ORS 659A.272.
38 “(23) ‘Self-employed individual’ means:
39 “(a) An individual who has self-employment income as defined in section 1402(b) of the Internal
40 Revenue Code as amended and in effect on December 31, [2023] 2025; or
41 “(b) An independent contractor as defined in ORS 670.600.
42 “(24) ‘Serious health condition’ means:
43 “(a) An illness, injury, impairment or physical or mental condition that requires inpatient care
44 in a hospital, hospice or residential medical care facility;
45 “(b) An illness, disease or condition that in the medical judgment of the treating health care
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 45

1 provider poses an imminent danger of death, is terminal in prognosis with a reasonable possibility
2 of death in the near future, or requires constant care;
3 “(c) Any period of disability due to pregnancy, or period of absence for prenatal care; or
4 “(d) Any period of absence for the donation of a body part, organ or tissue, including preoper-
5 ative or diagnostic services, surgery, post-operative treatment and recovery.
6 “(25) ‘Third party administrator’ means a third party that enters into an agreement with the
7 Director of the Employment Department to implement and administer the paid family and medical
8 leave program established under this chapter.
9 “(26) ‘Tribal government’ means:
10 “(a) A tribal government as defined in ORS 181A.940; or
11 “(b) A federally recognized Indian tribe.
12 “(27)(a) ‘Wages’ has the meaning given that term in ORS 657.105.
13 “(b) ‘Wages’ does not mean contribution amounts paid to the Paid Family and Medical Leave
14 Insurance Fund by an employer on behalf of an employee under ORS 657B.150 (5).
15 “SECTION 33. (1) Except as provided in subsections (2) and (3) of this section, the
16 amendments to statutes by sections 1 to 32 of this 2026 Act apply to transactions or activities
17 occurring on or after January 1, 2026, in tax years beginning on or after January 1, 2026.
18 “(2) The effective and applicable dates, and the exceptions, special rules and coordination
19 with the Internal Revenue Code, as amended, relative to those dates, contained in federal law
20 amending the Internal Revenue Code and enacted before January 1, 2026, apply for Oregon
21 personal income and corporate excise and income tax purposes, to the extent they can be
22 made applicable, in the same manner as they are applied under the Internal Revenue Code
23 and related federal law.
24 “(3)(a) If a deficiency is assessed against any taxpayer for a tax year beginning before
25 January 1, 2026, and the deficiency or any portion thereof is attributable to any retroactive
26 treatment under the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239, 305.494, 305.690, 305.842,
27 314.011, 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and 317A.100 by sections 1, 2
28 and 16 to 29 of this 2026 Act, then any interest or penalty assessed under ORS chapter 305,
29 314, 315, 316, 317, 317A or 318 with respect to the deficiency or portion thereof shall be can-
30 celed.
31 “(b) If a refund is due any taxpayer for a tax year beginning before January 1, 2026, and
32 the refund or any portion thereof is due the taxpayer on account of any retroactive treat-
33 ment under the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239, 305.494, 305.690, 305.842, 314.011,
34 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and 317A.100 by sections 1, 2 and 16
35 to 29 of this 2026 Act for a tax year beginning before January 1, 2026, then notwithstanding
36 ORS 305.270 or 314.415 or any other law, the refund or portion thereof shall be paid without
37 interest.
38 “(c) Any changes required because of the amendments to ORS 178.300, 178.375, 305.239,
39 305.494, 305.690, 305.842, 314.011, 314.306, 315.004, 316.012, 316.147, 316.157, 317.010, 317.097 and
40 317A.100 by sections 1, 2 and 16 to 29 of this 2026 Act for a tax year beginning before January
41 1, 2026, shall be made by filing an amended return within the time prescribed by law.
42 “(d) If a taxpayer fails to file an amended return under paragraph (c) of this subsection,
43 the Department of Revenue shall make any changes under paragraph (c) of this subsection
44 on the return to which the changes relate within the period specified for issuing a notice of
45 deficiency or claiming a refund as otherwise provided by law with respect to that return, or
SMRA to SB 1507 Page 46

1 within one year after a return for a tax year beginning on or after January 1, 2026, and be-
2 fore January 1, 2027, is filed, whichever period expires later.
3 “SECTION 34. ORS 315.266 is amended to read:
4 “315.266. (1)(a) In addition to any other credit available for purposes of ORS chapter 316, an
5 eligible resident individual shall be allowed a credit against the tax otherwise due under ORS
6 chapter 316 for the tax year in an amount equal to [nine] 14 percent of the earned income credit
7 allowable to the individual for the same tax year under section 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
8 “(b) Notwithstanding paragraph (a) of this subsection, for a taxpayer with a dependent under the
9 age of three at the close of the tax year, the credit allowed under this section shall be in an amount
10 equal to [12] 17 percent of the earned income credit allowable to the individual for the same tax
11 year under section 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
12 “(2) A resident individual may claim a credit under this section, using either a Social Security
13 number or an individual taxpayer identification number, if, but for section 32(m) of the Internal
14 Revenue Code, the individual would otherwise be eligible to claim a credit under section 32 of the
15 Internal Revenue Code. The credit allowed as provided in this subsection shall equal the percent-
16 age, as stated in subsection (1) of this section, of the amount that would be allowed on a federal
17 return, based on the amount of the individual’s earned income and the other provisions of section
18 32 of the Internal Revenue Code.
19 “(3) An eligible nonresident individual shall be allowed the credit computed in the same manner
20 and subject to the same limitations as the credit allowed a resident by subsection (1) or (2) of this
21 section. However, the credit shall be prorated using the proportion provided in ORS 316.117.
22 “(4) If a change in the taxable year of a taxpayer occurs as described in ORS 314.085, or if the
23 Department of Revenue terminates the taxpayer’s taxable year under ORS 314.440, the credit al-
24 lowed by this section shall be prorated or computed in a manner consistent with ORS 314.085.
25 “(5) If a change in the status of a taxpayer from resident to nonresident or from nonresident to
26 resident occurs, the credit allowed by this section shall be determined in a manner consistent with
27 ORS 316.117.
28 “(6) If the amount allowable as a credit under this section, when added to the sum of the
29 amounts allowable as payment of tax under ORS 316.187 or 316.583, other tax prepayment amounts
30 and other refundable credit amounts, exceeds the taxes imposed by ORS chapters 314 and 316 for
31 the tax year after application of any nonrefundable credits allowable for purposes of ORS chapter
32 316 for the tax year, the amount of the excess shall be refunded to the taxpayer as provided in ORS
33 316.502.
34 “(7) The Department of Revenue may adopt rules for purposes of this section, including but not
35 limited to rules relating to proof of eligibility, the furnishing of information regarding the federal
36 earned income credit claimed by the taxpayer for the tax year and policies and guidelines for the
37 determination of the amount of credit allowed under subsection (2) of this section.
38 “(8) Refunds attributable to the earned income credit allowed under this section do not bear
39 interest.
40 “SECTION 35. The amendments to ORS 315.266 by section 34 of this 2026 Act apply to tax
41 years beginning on or after January 1, 2026.
42 “SECTION 36. This 2026 Act takes effect on the 91st day after the date on which the 2026
43 regular session of the Eighty-third Legislative Assembly adjourns sine die.”.
